NEW YORK TIMES, AUGUST 30TH, 1968

Interview with President Humphrey

Governor Percy increasingly certain to be nominee

Democratic convention: excerpt from Senator Kennedy’s speech

So do not let them say the last eight years have been wasted. Let them not say our mission for the future is fruitless.

For another great task lies before us, to confront the poverty of satisfaction and hope. To confront a lack of purpose and dignity that threatens to infect us all. It is truly folly to believe that we can find such purpose and dignity in the mere accumulation of material possessions. Our gross national project us over eight hundred billion dollars. But this figure contains air pollution and cigarette advertising. It counts for ambulances, which day after day clear our highways of carnage. It counts special locks for our doors, for those Americans scared of their fellow man, and it counts jails for those who break them. It counts napalm and the cost of a nuclear warhead, and armoured cars for our police who fight riots in our very streets and television programs that glorify violence for mere profit.

And for all that it measures, it does not allow for the health of our children, the quality of their education, or the simple joy of their play. It does not include the beauty of our poetry or the strength of our marriages, the intelligence of our public officials or the intelligence of our public debate. It tells us everything about America except why we are proud to be Americans.

As you and I begin our national campaign to solve this crisis, let me quote George Bernard Shaw, Some men see things as they are, and say why. I dream of things that never were, and ask why not?

REPORT ON THE IMPLICATIONS OF JOHNSON'S THINNED MANDATE
